      <span class="bold">

      <br><span class="italic">Shandong Provincial Key Laboratory/Collaborative Innovation Center of Chemical Energy Storage &amp; Novel Cell Technology, School of Chemistry and Chemical Engineering, Liaocheng University, Liaocheng 252000, China. E-mail: <a href="mailto:lirui@lcu.edu.cn">lirui@lcu.edu.cn</a></span>
    </p><div id="art-admin"><span class="italic bold">Received 
      29th June 2022
    </span><span class="bold italic">, Accepted 6th October 2022</span></div><p class="bold italic">First published on 7th October 2022</p><hr><div class="abstract"><h2>Abstract</h2><p>Pillared MXenes with large interlayer spacing have shown great potential as an anode material for sodiumion batteries (SIBs). To better understand the underlying mechanism of the pillar effect in enhancing the electrochemical performance, first-principles calculations were used to investigate the adsorption and diffusion of Na in MXenes (Ti<small><sub>2</sub></small>CO<small><sub>2</sub></small> and Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small>), as well as the mechanical properties of the system under different MXenes layer spacings. The results showed that when the MXene layer spacing was 4 , the strongest adsorption of Na on MXenes was achieved due to the interlayer synergy effect. However, when the MXene layer spacing was greater than 5 , double Na-atomic layer adsorption would be formed, which increased the Na storage capacity. Interestingly, the diffusion of Na was not only affected by the interlayer spacing of MXenes, but also by the interlayer stacking mode of MXenes. Moreover, it was found that when the MXene layer spacing was more than 8 , the sodium storage properties basically did not change significantly. The optimal layer spacing for Ti<small><sub>2</sub></small>CO<small><sub>2</sub></small> and Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> was predicted to be 7 and 6 , respectively. This work provides valuable theoretical guidance for developing high-performance anode materials for SIBs.</p></div><hr>
    
      
      <h2 id="sect258"><span class="a_heading">1. Introduction</span></h2>
      <span>Lithiumion batteries (LIBs) are widely used in portable and intelligent electronic devices due to their comparative advantages of high energy density, excellent cycling stability and environmental friendliness.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit1"><sup><span class="sup_ref">1,2</span></sup></a> However, the limited natural reserves and the high mining cost of lithium make LIBs difficult to meet the growing demand of the battery market.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit3"><sup><span class="sup_ref">35</span></sup></a> Therefore, it is quite urgent to develop alternatives to the mainstream LIBs. Recently, due to the similar physical and chemical properties of both sodium and lithium, and the relatively rich reserves and wide distribution of sodium resources, sodiumion batteries (SIBs) have gradually attracted wide attention and are expected to replace LIBs in the field of medium and large scale energy storage applications.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit6"><sup><span class="sup_ref">69</span></sup></a> However, compared with lithium, sodium has a larger ionic radius, which leads to a slow reaction kinetics and huge volume expansion of the anode materials during the charging and discharging processes.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit10"><sup><span class="sup_ref">10,11</span></sup></a> Graphite and other materials that are commonly used in the anode of LIBs are difficult to be directly applied in SIBs.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit12"><sup><span class="sup_ref">1214</span></sup></a> Therefore, the design of high-capacity and long-cycle-life anode materials is considered of great significance for the development of SIBs.</span>
      <p class="otherpara">Due to their large specific surface area, the existence of many surface active sites, short ion transport path, and excellent mechanical and electrical properties, two-dimensional (2D) materials have emerged as potential candidates for the anode of SIBs.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit15"><sup><span class="sup_ref">1519</span></sup></a> In recent years, MXenes, with the general formula M<small><sub><span class="italic">n</span>+1</sub></small>X<small><sub><span class="italic">n</span></sub></small>T<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small> (where M represents the early transition metals, X denotes C and/or N, and T<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small> stands for the surface terminations and <span class="italic">n</span> = 1, 2, or 3), have attracted significant attention as a new family of 2D materials, and they have been a research hotspot in the energy storage field due to their fast response to the charge, pseudocapacitance characteristics and stable cycling performance.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit20"><sup><span class="sup_ref">2025</span></sup></a> Wang <span class="italic">et al.</span> found that compared with the raw material Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>AlC<small><sub>2</sub></small>, Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>X (X = OH, F, and O) MXene nanosheets exhibited significantly improved electrochemical performance for Na storage, showing excellent rate performance and long-term cycling stability, which was ascribed to the high electronic and ionic conductivity of MXenes.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit26"><sup><span class="sup_ref">26</span></sup></a> In another interesting work, Xie <span class="italic">et al.</span> reported that on the O-terminal MXene nanosheets, Na had moderate capacities with good rate capabilities. Therefore, O-terminated MXene nanosheets are promising electrode materials for SIBs.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit27"><sup><span class="sup_ref">27</span></sup></a></p>
      <p class="otherpara">However, when they are used as an anode electrode material for rechargeable batteries, MXene nanosheets usually suffer from aggregation and the self-restacking effect during the cycling process, which affects the ion transport properties, leading to lowered capacities, rate capabilities and cycling stabilities.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit28"><sup><span class="sup_ref">28,29</span></sup></a> Recently, an effective strategy has been proposed to overcome this shortcoming by fabricating pillared MXene structures with enlarged interlayer spacing. Lu <span class="italic">et al.</span> found that the intercalation of Al ions in a two-dimensional Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>T<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small> anode increased the spacing of the MXene layers by about 0.1 nm, and the lithium storage capacity and cycling stability of the MXene anode were also significantly improved.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit30"><sup><span class="sup_ref">30</span></sup></a> Luo <span class="italic">et al.</span> synthesized pillared Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small> with alkali metal ions (Li<small><sup>+</sup></small>, Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> and K<small><sup>+</sup></small>), in which the Na pillaring process increased the spacing of the MXene layer by about 0.3 nm. After testing, it was found that Na-Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>T<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small> has excellent Na storage capacity properties, and its capacity and kinetics were improved.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit31"><sup><span class="sup_ref">31</span></sup></a> Zhang <span class="italic">et al.</span> solved the agglomeration problem of MXenes by means of a NH<small><sub>4</sub></small><small><sup>+</sup></small>-based method, and successfully prepared Sn-based nanocomplex pillared few-layered Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>T<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small> composites.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit32"><sup><span class="sup_ref">32</span></sup></a> Benefiting from the pillar effect, the material exhibited excellent lithiumion storage and electrochemical performance, as well as remarkable cycling stability and rate capacity. Wang <span class="italic">et al.</span> developed VS<small><sub>4</sub></small> nanoarray pillared Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>T<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small> (VS<small><sub>4</sub></small>@L-Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>T<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>) using a facile hydrothermal approach. The test results revealed that a sodiumion half-cell based on the VS<small><sub>4</sub></small>@L-Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>T<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small> anode exhibited high specific capacity and good cycling performance. It was also proposed that the Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>T<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small> structure with enlarged interlayer spacing could facilitate fast reaction kinetics for both electron transportation and ion diffusion.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit33"><sup><span class="sup_ref">33</span></sup></a></p>
      <p class="otherpara">However, the basic mechanism of the MXene pillar effect enhancing the electrode performance of SIBs is still unclear. Under this direction, to better understand the pillar effect on the Na storage performance of MXenes, in this work, based on two typical MXenes (Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> and Ti<small><sub>2</sub></small>CO<small><sub>2</sub></small>), the impact of the different interlayer spacing and stacking modes between MXene sheets on the sodium storage performance was thoroughly investigated. In addition, various factors including Na adsorption, diffusion and mechanical properties were comprehensively considered and the optimum interlayer spacing of MXene sheets for Na storage was predicted. Our research provides valuable theoretical support for the development of high-efficiency pillared MXenes as electrode materials for SIB applications.</p>
    
    
      
      <h2 id="sect341"><span class="a_heading">2. Computational details</span></h2>
      <span>Here, according to the different research needs, a variety of MXene models were considered. More specifically, the MXene atomic layer of the primitive cell was located in the <span class="italic">x</span><span class="italic">y</span> plane (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig1">Fig. 1a and b</a>). In order to simulate an isolated single-layer MXene (MXene_IS) structure, a vacuum layer of 20  was set along the <span class="italic">z</span>-axis to avoid the interactions between the periodically repeated structures. The change of the MXene layer spacing was simulated by changing the vacuum layer thickness of the single-layer MXene model (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig1">Fig. 1c and d</a>). Each layer of the Ti<small><sub>2</sub></small>CO<small><sub>2</sub></small> was composed of a quintuple layer with OTiCTiO stacking modes, which can be regarded as C atomic layers sandwiched by two OTi layers, with the two O atoms located above the hollow sites of the bottom Ti atoms. The Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> monolayer consists of seven atomic layers of OTi(1)CTi(2)CTi(1)O, which can be regarded as a Ti(2) atomic layer sandwiched by two OTi(1)C layers, terminating the O atom in the hollow position of Ti(1). In order to simulate the adsorption of Na with different coverage properties, 2  2, 3  3, and 4  4 MXene supercell models were built, respectively. In addition, an isolated double-layer MXene model was also established, namely two layers of MXene were stacked in one cell box (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig1">Fig. 1e and f</a>) with a vacuum layer of 20  along the <span class="italic">z</span>-axis. All calculations were performed by using the Vienna <span class="italic">Ab initio</span> simulation package (VASP) based on density functional theory (DFT) with the projected augmented wave (PAW) method,<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit34"><sup><span class="sup_ref">34,35</span></sup></a> where a plane-wave cut-off energy of 500 eV was applied. The PerdewBurkeErnzerhof (PBE)<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit36"><sup><span class="sup_ref">36</span></sup></a> exchangecorrelation function of the generalized gradient approximation (GGA) was also selected for calculations. The Grimme DFT-D3<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit37"><sup><span class="sup_ref">37</span></sup></a> scheme of the dispersion correction with a zero damping coefficient was adopted to account for the van der Waals (vdW) interactions. When the thickness of the vacuum layer of the model was less than 9 , MonkhorstPack <span class="italic">K</span>-point meshes<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit38"><sup><span class="sup_ref">38</span></sup></a> with 8  8  2, 4  4  2, 3  3  2 and 2  2  2 were used to sample the Brillouin zone for the 1  1, 2  2, 3  3 and 4  4 supercell structures, respectively, whereas for the model with the vacuum layer greater than 9 , the <span class="italic">K</span>-point meshes along the <span class="italic">z</span>-axis were set to 1.</span>
      <br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgfig1"><a href="/image/article/2022/CP/d2cp02961h/d2cp02961h-f1_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d2cp02961h-f1.tif" src="/image/article/2022/CP/d2cp02961h/d2cp02961h-f1.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td class="image_title"><b>Fig. 1 </b> <span id="fig1"><span class="graphic_title">Depiction of the top view and labeled adsorption sites of the primitive cell of (a) Ti<small><sub>2</sub></small>CO<small><sub>2</sub></small> and (b) Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small>. Schematic illustration of the side view of the single-layer MXene model of (c) Ti<small><sub>2</sub></small>CO<small><sub>2</sub></small>-SL and (d) Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small>-SL, and the double-layer MXene model of (e) Ti<small><sub>2</sub></small>CO<small><sub>2</sub></small>-DL and (f) Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small>-DL.</span></span></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>
      <p class="otherpara">For the double-layer MXene, the adhesion energy of MXene layers (<span class="italic">E</span><small><sub>inter</sub></small>) was calculated by using the following formula:<br></p><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgugt1"><a href="/image/article/2022/CP/d2cp02961h/d2cp02961h-t1_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d2cp02961h-t1.tif" src="/image/article/2022/CP/d2cp02961h/d2cp02961h-t1.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td><a id="ugt1"><span id="ugt1"></span></a></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>where <span class="italic">E</span><small><sub>M1</sub></small>, <span class="italic">E</span><small><sub>M2</sub></small> and <span class="italic">E</span><small><sub>total</sub></small> represent the energies of the two MXene layers and the whole system, respectively, and <span class="italic">A</span> denotes the area of the interface. According to the formula, the existence of large <span class="italic">E</span><small><sub>inter</sub></small> leads to a stronger binding effect between the MXene layers. The adsorption energy per Na atom (<span class="italic">E</span><small><sub>a</sub></small>) was defined by the following formula:<br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgugt2"><a href="/image/article/2022/CP/d2cp02961h/d2cp02961h-t2_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d2cp02961h-t2.tif" src="/image/article/2022/CP/d2cp02961h/d2cp02961h-t2.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td><a id="ugt2"><span id="ugt2"></span></a></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>where <span class="italic">E</span><small><sub>MXene</sub></small> and <span class="italic">E</span><small><sub>Na</sub></small> represent the energy of the pristine MXene and Na, respectively. In addition, <span class="italic">n</span> is the number of absorbed Na atoms, and <span class="italic">E</span><small><sub>MXene+<span class="italic">n</span>Na</sub></small> is the energy of the entire Na-adsorbed system. Based on the above formula, a large value of <span class="italic">E</span><small><sub>a</sub></small> would represent the manifestation of a relatively stronger binding between Na and MXene.<p></p>
      <p class="otherpara">The climbing image nudged elastic band (CI-NEB) method<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit39"><sup><span class="sup_ref">39</span></sup></a> was used to explore the transition states for Na diffusion on MXenes and determine the diffusion energy barriers. The Na adsorption stability on the different sites was examined by performing <span class="italic">ab initio</span> molecular dynamic (AIMD) simulations. The simulations were performed considering the canonical ensemble <span class="italic">NVT</span> at 300 K, and simulation time was set at 20 ps with time steps of 1.0 fs. The mechanical properties including the elastic constants and Poisson's ratio were calculated using the VASPKIT code.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit40"><sup><span class="sup_ref">40</span></sup></a></p>
    
    
      
      <h2 id="sect413"><span class="a_heading">3. Results and discussion</span></h2>
      
        
        <h3 id="sect416"><span class="b_heading">3.1 Adsorption of Na on isolated MXene</span></h3>
        <span>Firstly, the MXene_IS models were fully optimized, and the optimized single-layer thickness values of Ti<small><sub>2</sub></small>CO<small><sub>2</sub></small> and Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> were 4.37  and 7.07 , respectively. In the experiment, the restacking effect of the MXene nanosheets is usually inevitable, resulting in a too-small layer spacing, which could significantly weaken the electrode performance. However, the MXene layer spacing can be adjusted by introducing other molecules, while the layer spacing varies with the size of the introduced molecules.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit41"><sup><span class="sup_ref">4143</span></sup></a> Here, MXene structures with different layer spacings were simulated by changing the vacuum layer thickness of the single-layer MXene models (Ti<small><sub>2</sub></small>CO<small><sub>2</sub></small>-SL and Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small>-SL). The extracted results show that when the thickness of the vacuum layer is changed, the thickness of the optimized MXene sheet will also change slightly. As a result, the layer spacing will be slightly different from the initial setting (see Table S1 in the ESI<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a>). However, the recorded differences are negligible and no obvious change is detected when the layer spacing was larger than 7 . The same situation also appeared in the isolated double-layer MXene models (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig1">Fig. 1e and f</a>) when the layer spacing of the double-layer MXene was changed. In addition, the adhesion energy between MXene layers with different layer spacing was calculated for Ti<small><sub>2</sub></small>CO<small><sub>2</sub></small>-DL, and Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small>-DL, respectively. When the layer spacing was 3 , the calculated adhesion energy was 2.5 eV nm<small><sup>2</sup></small>, which shows the development of a typical vdW interaction.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit44"><sup><span class="sup_ref">44</span></sup></a> It is obvious that the adhesion energy is decreased with the increase of layer spacing, and there is almost no interaction at a distance of 12  (Fig. S1, ESI<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a>). This effect also confirms that it is appropriate for us to set 20  vacuum layer to simulate an isolated MXene system.</span>
        <p class="otherpara">Next, Na adsorption on MXene_IS was systematically studied. Under this direction, three different adsorption sites were investigated, namely the O site at the top of the atomic layer, the Ti site at the second atomic layer and the C site at the third atomic layer (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig1">Fig. 1a and b</a>). The adsorption energy is shown in <a title="Select to navigate to table" href="#tab1">Table 1</a>. The extracted results indicate that in both 1  1 and 2  2 supercells, the preferable Na adsorption site is the C site, and the order of adsorption energy at the three sites is as follows: C &gt; Ti &gt; O. To test the stability of Na at these adsorption sites, MD simulations of Na adsorption on the 2  2 MXene_IS were also conducted, where the Na coverage was 1/4 ML. In the MD simulation, three adsorption sites were selected as the initial adsorption sites of Na, respectively. Fig. S2 (ESI<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a>) shows the change in the distance in the <span class="italic">x</span><span class="italic">y</span> plane between Na and the initial and final adsorption sites along the simulation time. It was found that Na could be stably adsorbed at the initial C site, while for the initial adsorption site Ti or O was selected, Na would be transferred to the adjacent C site after a period of simulation. All the above mentioned results indicate that the most stable adsorption site for Na was determined as the C site. Therefore, for subsequent research on the Na adsorption properties, only the C adsorption site was considered.</p>

          <hr class="hrule"><br>
        <p class="otherpara">Furthermore, the adsorption of single Na on 3  3 and 4  4 supercells of MXene_IS was investigated. It was found that compared with 1  1 and 2  2 systems, the adsorption energy of Na was larger in the 3  3 and 4  4 supercells. In particular in the 4  4 supercell, the adsorption energy of Na was increased by nearly 2 eV compared with the 1  1 system. The adsorption of single Na in the four models represents different amounts of Na coverage, that is to say, the Na coverage was 1 ML, 1/4 ML,1/9 ML and 1/16 ML, respectively. These results indicate that the adsorption energy decreased with the increase of Na coverage, which shows the repulsion between Na.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit24"><sup><span class="sup_ref">24</span></sup></a> It was also found that compared with the Ti<small><sub>2</sub></small>CO<small><sub>2</sub></small> structure, Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> has a greater adsorption capacity for Na, which is consistent with the results of the previously reported studies.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit26"><sup><span class="sup_ref">26,27,45</span></sup></a></p>
      
      
        
        <h3 id="sect545"><span class="b_heading">3.2 Impact of MXene layer spacing on Na adsorption</span></h3>
        <span>The impact of MXene layer spacing on the Na adsorption under 1 ML Na coverage (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig2">Fig. 2</a>) was also examined. Previous studies suggest that the interlayer spacing of MXene could be enlarged <span class="italic">via</span> the introduction of intercalation agents, and the range of layer spacing change is very wide with different intercalation agents.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit46"><sup><span class="sup_ref">46</span></sup></a> Here, we set different interlayer spacings at an interval of 0.5 or 1 , which was convenient to draw the adsorption curve of Na under different MXene interlayer spacings, so as to investigate the influence of different interlayer spacing on Na adsorption. More specifically, 10 different interlayer distance values (3, 3.5, 4, 4.5, 5, 5.5, 6, 7, 8, and 9 ) were selected, respectively, and the Na adsorption configurations and energies were studied. All adsorption energy data are listed in Table S2 (ESI<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a>), and the trend of the adsorption energy change with the layer spacing is shown in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig3">Fig. 3</a>. From the extracted outcomes, it can be argued that the adsorption energy curve of Na presenting a parabolic profile can be detected. With the increase of the layer spacing, the adsorption energy of Na was first increased and then decreased. In the beginning, due to the synergistic adsorption effect of both the upper and lower MXene layers (for convenience, the two adjacent layers of MXene are referred to as upper and lower layers, as shown in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig2">Fig. 2</a>), the <span class="italic">E</span><small><sub>a</sub></small> value was relatively large and reached the maximum value at about 4 . After that, <span class="italic">E</span><small><sub>a</sub></small> began to decline with the increase of layer spacing. However, when the layer spacing was more than 6 , no significant changes in the <span class="italic">E</span><small><sub>a</sub></small> value were detected. At this point, Na was adsorbed on the lower MXene layer and was far away from the upper MXene layer. As a result, it was difficult to be affected by the upper MXene layer. On the other hand, when the layer spacing reached a value of 9 , the adsorption energy of Na on Ti<small><sub>2</sub></small>CO<small><sub>2</sub></small> and Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> was 1.95 eV and 2.24 eV, respectively, which was consistent with respective values that were calculated on the isolated single-layer MXene, indicating that Na was only affected by the lower layer of MXene. In addition, the adsorption of Na in the 1  1 bilayer-based MXene (Ti<small><sub>2</sub></small>CO<small><sub>2</sub></small>-DL and Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small>-DL) model was also studied. By changing the distance between the two layers of MXene along the <span class="italic">z</span>-axis, the changing of the layer spacing was simulated. It is found that the change in the trend of the adsorption energy is consistent with that of the monolayer model (Fig. S3, ESI<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a>), suggesting that the proposed method of changing the vacuum layer is suitable to simulate the change of the MXene layer spacing in the single-layer model.</span>
        <br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgfig2"><a href="/image/article/2022/CP/d2cp02961h/d2cp02961h-f2_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d2cp02961h-f2.tif" src="/image/article/2022/CP/d2cp02961h/d2cp02961h-f2.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td class="image_title"><b>Fig. 2 </b> <span id="fig2"><span class="graphic_title">Schematic diagram of the Na adsorption in MXene sheets with different stacking modes: (a) Ti<small><sub>2</sub></small>CO<small><sub>2</sub></small> with CC stacking, (b) Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> with CC stacking, (c) Ti<small><sub>2</sub></small>CO<small><sub>2</sub></small> with CTi stacking and (d) Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> with CTi stacking.</span></span></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>
        <br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgfig3"><a href="/image/article/2022/CP/d2cp02961h/d2cp02961h-f3_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d2cp02961h-f3.tif" src="/image/article/2022/CP/d2cp02961h/d2cp02961h-f3.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td class="image_title"><b>Fig. 3 </b> <span id="fig3"><span class="graphic_title">Change of the Na adsorption energy with layer spacing in the single-layer MXene model (a) Ti<small><sub>2</sub></small>CO<small><sub>2</sub></small>-SL and (b) Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small>-SL.</span></span></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>
        <p class="otherpara">The change of Na adsorption energy with layer spacing under other Na coverages (1/4 ML, 1/9 ML, and 1/16 ML) was also investigated. It was found that the change of the adsorption energy has the same trend under all Na coverages (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig3">Fig. 3</a>). However, with the decrease of the coverage, the Na adsorption energy was increased obviously. Furthermore, when the Na coverage was reduced to 1/9 ML, the Na adsorption energy was comparable to that of 1/16 ML. The acquired results revealed that the maximum adsorption energy under all Na coverage conditions occurs at about 4  of the MXene layer spacing. When the interlayer distance was less than 4 , the MXene structures were prone to slight deformation, which resulted in unstable Na adsorption. On the other hand, when the interval between MXene layers was larger than 4 , the synergistic adsorption effect between MXene layers was weakened, which also resulted in a decrease of the Na adsorption energy. This result indicates that, by considering only the adsorption energy, the most suitable spacing of the MXene layer for Na adsorption should be about 4 .</p>
        <p class="otherpara">Besides the change in the adsorption energy, it was found that the distance between Na and its C adsorption site (<span class="italic">d</span><small><sub>NaC</sub></small>) was also changed with the layer spacing (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig4">Fig. 4</a>). As can be seen from <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig4">Fig. 4</a>, the change of <span class="italic">d</span><small><sub>NaC</sub></small> has the same tendency in both Ti<small><sub>2</sub></small>CO<small><sub>2</sub></small> and Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small>. More specifically, when the layer spacing was small (less than 5 ), <span class="italic">d</span><small><sub>NaC</sub></small> increased gradually as the layer spacing became bigger. After the layer spacing reached the value of 5 , <span class="italic">d</span><small><sub>NaC</sub></small> gradually decreased and basically did not change after reaching 8 . Similar trends under the four Na coverage conditions were observed, however, slightly different. In the case of 1/9 and 1/16 ML Na coverage, <span class="italic">d</span><small><sub>NaC</sub></small> reached the maximum value at a layer spacing of 5 . Under these layer spacing conditions, for Ti<small><sub>2</sub></small>CO<small><sub>2</sub></small>, the <span class="italic">d</span><small><sub>NaC</sub></small> was about 0.5  larger than that of the isolated single-layer MXene, and for Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small>, it was increased by about 0.6  compared with the isolated system. In the case of high Na coverage (1 ML and 1/4 ML), <span class="italic">d</span><small><sub>NaC</sub></small> reached the maximum value when the MXene layer spacing was 4.5 , which was slightly different from the case where a low Na coverage was used. Moreover, compared with the low Na coverage, the variation of <span class="italic">d</span><small><sub>NaC</sub></small> with the layer spacing under high Na coverage was smaller.</p>
        <br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgfig4"><a href="/image/article/2022/CP/d2cp02961h/d2cp02961h-f4_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d2cp02961h-f4.tif" src="/image/article/2022/CP/d2cp02961h/d2cp02961h-f4.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td class="image_title"><b>Fig. 4 </b> <span id="fig4"><span class="graphic_title">Change of the NaC distance with layer spacing in the single-layer MXene model (a) Ti<small><sub>2</sub></small>CO<small><sub>2</sub></small>-SL and (b) Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small>-SL.</span></span></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>
        <p class="otherpara">Similarly, this change in the NaC distance with the MXene layer spacing is also due to the synergistic effect of the two MXene layers on Na. When the interval between MXene layers was less than 5 , the adsorption position of Na tends to be located in the middle of the two MXene layers due to the synergistic effect of the two MXene layers. However, after the layer spacing reaches a value of 5 , the synergistic effect of the two MXene layers becomes weak. Consequently, Na is only adsorbed on the lower layer of MXene, and is no longer affected by the upper layer of MXene. This deduction can also be obtained by analyzing the electron-density difference plots of the Na adsorption. As shown in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig5">Fig. 5</a>, compared with the small layer spacing case, when the layer spacing was increased to 5 , the electronic interaction between Na and the upper MXene layer had been weakened. When the layer spacing reached a value of 6 , no electronic interaction between Na and the upper MXene layer was basically detected.</p>
        <br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgfig5"><a href="/image/article/2022/CP/d2cp02961h/d2cp02961h-f5_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d2cp02961h-f5.tif" src="/image/article/2022/CP/d2cp02961h/d2cp02961h-f5.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td class="image_title"><b>Fig. 5 </b> <span id="fig5"><span class="graphic_title">Electron-density differences of Na adsorption in Ti<small><sub>2</sub></small>CO<small><sub>2</sub></small> sheets with layer spacings of (a) 3 , (b) 4 , (c) 5  and (d) 6 . The cyan and yellow isosurfaces represent the depletion and accumulation of electrons, respectively. The isosurface value was 3  10<small><sup>3</sup></small> e <small><sup>3</sup></small>.</span></span></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>
        <p class="otherpara">The adsorption energy of Na decreased with the increase of the coverage, which could be attributed to the repulsion of Na. However, the extracted results showed the existence of a certain difference in this trend with different layer spacings (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig6">Fig. 6</a>). On top of that, when the layer spacing was less than 5 , the adsorption energy decreased slowly with the increase of Na coverage. Even when it was changed from 1/4 to 1 ML, the adsorption energy was not affected dramatically. When the layer spacing was increased to 6 , the change of the adsorption energy was still very small when the Na coverage changed from 1/16 to 1/4 ML. However, when the Na coverage changed from 1/4 to 1 ML, the adsorption energy decreased dramatically. This effect suggests that when the interlayer spacing was small, the repulsion between Na may be weakened by the interlayer synergy effect of MXene.</p>
        <br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgfig6"><a href="/image/article/2022/CP/d2cp02961h/d2cp02961h-f6_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d2cp02961h-f6.tif" src="/image/article/2022/CP/d2cp02961h/d2cp02961h-f6.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td class="image_title"><b>Fig. 6 </b> <span id="fig6"><span class="graphic_title">Variation of the Na adsorption energy with Na coverage at different layer spacings in (a) Ti<small><sub>2</sub></small>CO<small><sub>2</sub></small> and (b)Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small>.</span></span></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>
        <p class="otherpara">In addition, the mechanical properties of the Na adsorption system under the high Na coverage (1 ML) were studied, which are considered quite important factors for the structural stability during the chargedischarge cycling process. First, the mechanical properties of the pristine isolated Ti<small><sub>2</sub></small>CO<small><sub>2</sub></small> and Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> structures were calculated and compared with the previously calculated values for validation. The calculated in-plane planar elastic constants <span class="italic">C</span><small><sub>11</sub></small> of both Ti<small><sub>2</sub></small>CO<small><sub>2</sub></small> and Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> were 268 N m<small><sup>1</sup></small> and 363 N m<small><sup>1</sup></small>, respectively, whereas their Poisson's ratios (<span class="italic">v</span>) were 0.302 and 0.291, respectively. The acquired data are in good agreement with the reported values in the literature,<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit47"><sup><span class="sup_ref">47,48</span></sup></a> so it can be concluded that the present DFT method can provide reliable results. After the adsorption of Na on the isolated MXene, the mechanical properties of the whole system were changed. Our results indicated that, compared with the pristine MXene, the <span class="italic">C</span><small><sub>11</sub></small> values of the MXeneNa system were increased, while the Poisson's ratios were decreased. For the Ti<small><sub>2</sub></small>CO<small><sub>2</sub></small>Na system, the calculated <span class="italic">C</span><small><sub>11</sub></small> and Poisson's ratios were 292 N m<small><sup>1</sup></small> and 0.258, respectively, and for the Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small>Na-based system, the calculated <span class="italic">C</span><small><sub>11</sub></small> and Poisson's ratio were 394 N m<small><sup>1</sup></small> and 0.241, respectively. The mechanical properties of the MXeneNa systems were also calculated with different MXene layer spacings, and all the data are listed in Table S3 (ESI<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a>). It was found that the mechanical properties of the whole system change with the change of the MXene layer spacing. From 39  layer spacing, both <span class="italic">C</span><small><sub>11</sub></small> and Poisson's ratios were decreased at first and reached a minimum when the layer spacing was 5 . Then, they gradually increased, and when the layer spacing reached a value of 9 , the mechanical properties no longer changed significantly (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig7">Fig. 7</a>).</p>
        <br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgfig7"><a href="/image/article/2022/CP/d2cp02961h/d2cp02961h-f7_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d2cp02961h-f7.tif" src="/image/article/2022/CP/d2cp02961h/d2cp02961h-f7.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td class="image_title"><b>Fig. 7 </b> <span id="fig7"><span class="graphic_title">Histograms of the change of (a) elastic constants <span class="italic">C</span><small><sub>11</sub></small>, and (b) Poisson's ratio of the MXeneNa system with layer spacing under 1 ML Na coverage.</span></span></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>
        <p class="otherpara">In our single-layer and double-layer MXene models, two adjacent layers of MXene were arranged in the same way along the <span class="italic">z</span>-axis. For the Ti<small><sub>2</sub></small>CO<small><sub>2</sub></small> structure, the adsorption site C of the lower MXene layer and the C of the upper MXene layer are arranged in a line along the <span class="italic">z</span>-axis (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig2">Fig. 2a</a>). Here, for convenience, this stacking mode is called CC stacking. In this mode, when Na is intercalated between the two layers of Ti<small><sub>2</sub></small>CO<small><sub>2</sub></small>, both the upper and the lower directions are affected by the favorable adsorption sites. As far as Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> is concerned, the adsorption site C of the lower MXene and Ti of the upper MXene are in a straight line along the <span class="italic">z</span>-axis, which is called the CTi stacking mode (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig2">Fig. 2d</a>). Therefore, when Na is adsorbed on the C site of the lower Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small>, it interacts with the Ti site of the upper layer of Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small>. Actually, MXene may shift and adopt different stacking modes during the stacking process.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit49"><sup><span class="sup_ref">49</span></sup></a> Therefore, it is necessary to investigate the influence of different stacking modes on Na adsorption. Here, other stacking models for Ti<small><sub>2</sub></small>CO<small><sub>2</sub></small> and Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> were considered, and the adsorption of Na on them was studied. For the Ti<small><sub>2</sub></small>CO<small><sub>2</sub></small> structure, the CTi stacking double-layer MXene models were constructed (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig2">Fig. 2b</a>), while for Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small>, the CC stacking double-layer MXene models were constructed (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig2">Fig. 2c</a>). It was found that the adsorption energy of Na in these models was slightly different from that in the previously reported models (Table S4, ESI<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a>). Moreover, the variation trend of the adsorption energy with MXene layer spacing was the same as that in the previous models, and the maximum Na adsorption energy also appeared when the MXene layer spacing was 4 . This outcome suggests that the change of the stacking mode of MXene has a negligible impact on the Na adsorption properties.</p>
      
      
        
        <h3 id="sect718"><span class="b_heading">3.3 Impact of the MXene layer spacing on Na diffusion</span></h3>
        <span>The performance of Na diffusion in the electrode material has also a direct impact on the chargedischarge efficiency of the SIBs.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit50"><sup><span class="sup_ref">50</span></sup></a> Therefore, the diffusion of Na between MXene layers and the impact of the MXene layer spacing on Na diffusion were thoroughly investigated. Under this perspective, the 2  2 MXene model was used to perform CI-NEB calculations for Na diffusion, and the adsorption configurations of Na at the two adjacent C sites were selected as the initial and final states on the Na diffusion pathway, respectively. Firstly, the diffusion of Na on isolated MXene was examined. It was found that the diffusion path of Na between the adjacent C sites was not a straight line, but through the adjacent Ti site (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig8">Fig. 8a and b</a>), which is consistent with the previously reported studies.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit51"><sup><span class="sup_ref">51,52</span></sup></a> The energy barriers for Na diffusion (EB<small><sub>d</sub></small>) on both Ti<small><sub>2</sub></small>CO<small><sub>2</sub></small> and Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> were 0.25 and 0.27 eV, respectively. This result is in good agreement with previous studies.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit27"><sup><span class="sup_ref">27,52</span></sup></a> The existence of such low energy barriers is conducive to Na diffusion on the MXene surface.</span>
        <br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgfig8"><a href="/image/article/2022/CP/d2cp02961h/d2cp02961h-f8_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d2cp02961h-f8.tif" src="/image/article/2022/CP/d2cp02961h/d2cp02961h-f8.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td class="image_title"><b>Fig. 8 </b> <span id="fig8"><span class="graphic_title">Schematic representation of Na diffusion path on the isolated MXene surface with a top view of (a) Ti<small><sub>2</sub></small>CO<small><sub>2</sub></small> and (b) Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small>, between two layers of MXene sheets with a side view of (c) CC stacking of Ti<small><sub>2</sub></small>CO<small><sub>2</sub></small>, (d) CTi stacking of Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small>, (e) CTi stacking of Ti<small><sub>2</sub></small>CO<small><sub>2</sub></small> and (f) CC stacking of Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small>.</span></span></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>
        <p class="otherpara">Furthermore, the diffusion of Na in MXene with different interlayer spacings was examined, and the corresponding energy barriers are displayed in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig9">Fig. 9</a>. The results showed that for the Ti<small><sub>2</sub></small>CO<small><sub>2</sub></small> structure, the EB<small><sub>d</sub></small> was quite large when the MXene interlayer spacing was low. More specifically, when the spacing between MXene layers was 3 , the extracted EB<small><sub>d</sub></small> value was as high as 2.11 eV, suggesting that Na was difficult to diffuse between MXene layers under such conditions. When the MXene layer spacing was increased from 3  to 6 , the EB<small><sub>d</sub></small> value gradually decreased. Interestingly, when the layer spacing was increased more than 6 , the EB<small><sub>d</sub></small> value no longer changed significantly and was very close to the EB<small><sub>d</sub></small> value of the isolated MXene.</p>
        <br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgfig9"><a href="/image/article/2022/CP/d2cp02961h/d2cp02961h-f9_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d2cp02961h-f9.tif" src="/image/article/2022/CP/d2cp02961h/d2cp02961h-f9.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td class="image_title"><b>Fig. 9 </b> <span id="fig9"><span class="graphic_title">Distribution of the energy barrier profiles of Na diffusion under different interlayer spacings in (a) CC stacking of Ti<small><sub>2</sub></small>CO<small><sub>2</sub></small>, (b) CTi stacking of Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small>, (c) CTi stacking of Ti<small><sub>2</sub></small>CO<small><sub>2</sub></small> and (d) CC stacking of Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small>.</span></span></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>
        <p class="otherpara">For the Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> configuration, the change in the EB<small><sub>d</sub></small> value with MXene layer spacing was completely different from Ti<small><sub>2</sub></small>CO<small><sub>2</sub></small>. As can be ascertained from <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig9">Fig. 9</a>, at a small layer spacing, the acquired EB<small><sub>d</sub></small> values on Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> were much lower than those on Ti<small><sub>2</sub></small>CO<small><sub>2</sub></small>. When the MXene layer spacing was 3 , the EB<small><sub>d</sub></small> value was only about 0.34 eV, while on increasing the MXene layer spacing to 45 , the EB<small><sub>d</sub></small> value became lower and was about 0.14 eV. As the spacing between the layers continued to increase, the EB<small><sub>d</sub></small> value gradually increased until the spacing reached 8 . On top of that, the EB<small><sub>d</sub></small> value under such conditions was close to that on isolated Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small>.</p>
        <p class="otherpara">Such a large contrast in Na diffusion between Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> and Ti<small><sub>2</sub></small>CO<small><sub>2</sub></small> structures could be due to different stacking modes of the layers. In particular, when the MXene layer spacing was small, the influence of the upper MXene on Na diffusion between the various MXene layers varies with the stacking modes. In the initial Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> model, the CTi stacking mode was adopted between the MXene layers. As far as the Na diffusion path in the Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> layers is concerned (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig8">Fig. 8d</a>), Na will pass through the adjacent Ti site of the lower layer, where the favorable C adsorption site of the upper layer is just above it (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig8">Fig. 8d</a>). As a result, this synergistic effect could greatly reduce the value of EB<small><sub>d</sub></small>. While for the Ti<small><sub>2</sub></small>CO<small><sub>2</sub></small> structure, the CC stacking mode was adopted, the Na diffusion path will be affected by the poor O adsorption site of the upper layer (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig8">Fig. 8c</a>), which makes the energy barrier relatively high.</p>
        <p class="otherpara">To further verify this assumption, the Na diffusion mechanisms in Ti<small><sub>2</sub></small>CO<small><sub>2</sub></small> with the CTi stacking mode and Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> with the CC stacking mode, respectively, were investigated. In the CTi stacking model of the Ti<small><sub>2</sub></small>CO<small><sub>2</sub></small> structure, the Na diffusion was affected by the C adsorption site of the upper MXene on the diffusion path (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig8">Fig. 8e</a>). Therefore, the EB<small><sub>d</sub></small> values were similar to those of the CTi stacking model of the Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> configuration (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig9">Fig. 9c</a>). On the other hand, in the CC stacking model of the Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> structure, the Na diffusion was affected by the existence of O sites in the upper MXene (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig8">Fig. 8f</a>), resulting in a similar EB<small><sub>d</sub></small> value to the CC stacking mode of Ti<small><sub>2</sub></small>CO<small><sub>2</sub></small> (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig9">Fig. 9d</a>). This effect suggests that, besides layer spacing, the stacking modes of MXene layers also have a great impact on the diffusion mechanism of Na between layers. In addition, our results also indicated that when the layer spacing of MXene reached a value of 7 , the EB<small><sub>d</sub></small> value basically did not change. Thus, it can be argued that when the MXene layer spacing was greater than 7 , the diffusion of Na was no longer affected by the upper MXene layer.</p>
      
      
        
        <h3 id="sect832"><span class="b_heading">3.4 Double-layer Na adsorption in MXenes</span></h3>
        <span>As far as the adsorption of Na between MXene layers is concerned, another situation should be considered, which is the double Na-atomic layer adsorption. It has been reported in the literature that double Na layers can be formed in the Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>X interlayer upon extensive Na intercalation,<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit26"><sup><span class="sup_ref">26</span></sup></a> which can lead to high capacity. However, this effect can only occur if the layer spacing is large. For that reason, the tests for different layer spacings were carried out by using the 2  2 supercell model of the Ti<small><sub>2</sub></small>CO<small><sub>2</sub></small> structure. Four Na atoms were intercalated between MXene layers, which was consistent with the number of Na at 1 ML coverage on the single-layer MXene. In order to obtain the structure of the double-layer Na adsorption under different layer spacings, in the initial structure, two Na were placed at the C site of the lower layer and the other two were placed at the C site of the upper layer. Additionally, the MXene layer spacing was set to values of 4, 5, 6, 7, 8 and 9 , respectively.</span>
        <p class="otherpara">The optimized structures showed that when the MXene layer spacing was 4 , four Na atoms could only form a single Na-atomic layer in the MXene interlayer due to the small layer spacing (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig10">Fig. 10a</a>). Moreover, Na was adsorbed at the center of the two MXene layers along the <span class="italic">z</span>-direction, and the adsorption energy of Na was 4.09 eV, which is consistent with the Na adsorption energy under 1 ML coverage. When the layer spacing was greater than 5 , double Na-atomic layers could be formed (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig10">Fig. 10b</a>), whereas the adsorption energies were 3.25, 2.31, 2.25 and 2.27 eV per Na at interlayer spacings of 5, 6, 7 and 8 , respectively. Compared with the adsorption energy of the single Na-atomic layer with a coverage of 1 ML, the adsorption energy of the double Na-atomic layer was generally larger under the same MXene layer spacing. This is because the distance between Na atoms is increased during the formation of the double Na-atomic layer, which weakens the rejection effect between Na atoms. Therefore, with the same number of Na adsorbed, the double Na-atomic layer structure tends to be formed when the spacing between MXene layers is greater than 5 .</p>
        <br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgfig10"><a href="/image/article/2022/CP/d2cp02961h/d2cp02961h-f10_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d2cp02961h-f10.tif" src="/image/article/2022/CP/d2cp02961h/d2cp02961h-f10.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td class="image_title"><b>Fig. 10 </b> <span id="fig10"><span class="graphic_title">Optimized structures of Na adsorption in a 2  2 supercell of Ti<small><sub>2</sub></small>CO<small><sub>2</sub></small> with an interlayer spacing of (a) 4  and (b) 5 .</span></span></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>
        <p class="otherpara">The double Na-atomic layer adsorption in the 1  1 MXene model was also investigated. More specifically, two Na atoms were inserted into the 1  1 MXene model, which was consistent with the number of Na at 2 ML coverage on the single-layer MXene. Na was adsorbed at the C sites of the lower and upper layer, respectively (Fig. S4, ESI<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a>), and five interlayer distances (5, 6, 7, 8, and 9 ) were considered. The extracted <span class="italic">E</span><small><sub>a</sub></small> values of all structures are listed in <a title="Select to navigate to table" href="#tab2">Table 2</a>. Compared with the single-layer Na adsorption energy, the <span class="italic">E</span><small><sub>a</sub></small> values of the double Na-atomic layers were significantly lower at a MXene layer spacing of 5 , and this result could be attributed to the repulsion effect between Na atoms. With the further increase of the layer spacing, the <span class="italic">E</span><small><sub>a</sub></small> could be increased due to the elongated NaNa distance. For the Ti<small><sub>2</sub></small>CO<small><sub>2</sub></small> structure, when the layer spacing was 7 , the interatomic distance of the two Na layers (<span class="italic">d</span><small><sub>NaNa</sub></small>) was 3.52 , and the <span class="italic">E</span><small><sub>a</sub></small> value reached the maximum (<a title="Select to navigate to table" href="#tab2">Table 2</a>), which was 2.13 eV per Na. In addition, when the layer spacing reached 9 , the <span class="italic">d</span><small><sub>NaNa</sub></small> was 5.5 . We have calculated the interaction energy between two Na atoms as a function of NaNa distance (Fig. S5, ESI<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a>), and the result showed that the interaction between Na atoms was very small when the NaNa distance reached 5.5 . The calculated <span class="italic">E</span><small><sub>a</sub></small> was 1.89 eV, which was similar to the <span class="italic">E</span><small><sub>a</sub></small> value of 1 ML Na coverage. On the other hand, for the Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> structure, the maximum <span class="italic">E</span><small><sub>a</sub></small> appeared when the layer spacing was 6 , and the <span class="italic">d</span><small><sub>NaNa</sub></small> was 3.43 . When the layer spacing reached 8 , the <span class="italic">d</span><small><sub>NaNa</sub></small> was 5.1 , and <span class="italic">E</span><small><sub>a</sub></small> was no longer changed.</p>
        
<div class="table_caption"><b>Table 2</b> <span id="tab2">The adsorption energy of the double Na-atomic layers on the 1  1 MXene model with different layer spacing</span>
		</div>

          <hr class="hrule"><br>
        <p class="otherpara">In addition to the adsorption characteristics, the mechanical properties of the double-layer Na adsorption system in the 1  1 MXene model also were further explored, and the calculated data are listed in Table S3 (ESI<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a>). Different from the Na monolayer adsorption, with the increase of the layer spacing, the elastic constant <span class="italic">C</span><small><sub>11</sub></small> of the double-layer Na adsorption system tends to decrease. On the other hand, their Poisson's ratio also decreased with the increase of layer spacing, and remained unchanged after 8 . The calculation of small Poisson's ratio represents better material robustness,<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit53"><sup><span class="sup_ref">53</span></sup></a> which suggests that the MXene structure with bilayer Na adsorption should be more robust at a large layer spacing.</p>
        <p class="otherpara">In order to determine the most suitable MXene layer spacing for the anode material of SIBs, various factors need to be comprehensively considered, including Na adsorption, diffusion, material stability, and so on. Here, based on our calculation results, four layer spacings (5, 6, 7, 8 ) were simply compared by plotting a radar chart (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig11">Fig. 11</a>). The double Na-atomic layers could be formed under all these four layer spacing conditions, which could achieve high capacities. In addition, a layer spacing greater than 8  was not considered since from the acquired calculation results it can be argued that when the MXene layer spacing was greater than 8 , the adsorption and diffusion of Na, as well as the mechanical properties, basically did not change. In this way, by increasing the layer spacing, the performance of the electrode material is not anticipated to be improved, but only increases the volume. Five different aspects are considered in the radar chart including <span class="italic">E</span><small><sub>a</sub></small> of the double Na-atomic layers, EB<small><sub>d</sub></small> of CC stacking, EB<small><sub>d</sub></small> of CTi stacking, the elastic constant <span class="italic">C</span><small><sub>11</sub></small> of the double-layer Na adsorption system, and the Poisson's ratio <span class="italic">v</span>. All data were normalized by the Minmax standardization method (see details in Table S5 in the ESI<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a>). The acquired normalized values are in the range of [0, 1] and the bigger value indicates a higher score. Therefore, a larger area in the radar chart indicates a better performance of the material, in terms of anode material for SIBs. As shown in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig11">Fig. 11</a>, for the Ti<small><sub>2</sub></small>CO<small><sub>2</sub></small> structure, the most suitable layer spacing should be 7 , while for the Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> configuration, the most suitable layer spacing was 6 .</p>
        <br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgfig11"><a href="/image/article/2022/CP/d2cp02961h/d2cp02961h-f11_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d2cp02961h-f11.tif" src="/image/article/2022/CP/d2cp02961h/d2cp02961h-f11.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td class="image_title"><b>Fig. 11 </b> <span id="fig11"><span class="graphic_title">Radar diagram for evaluating the optimal layer spacing of (a) Ti<small><sub>2</sub></small>CO<small><sub>2</sub></small> and (b) Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small>. <span class="italic">E</span><small><sub>a</sub></small> represents the adsorption energy of per Na atom in the double-layer Na adsorption system. EB<small><sub>d</sub></small> (CC stacking) represents the energy barriers of Na diffusion with CC stacking mode. EB<small><sub>d</sub></small> (CTi stacking) represents the energy barriers of Na diffusion with CTi stacking mode. <span class="italic">C</span><small><sub>11</sub></small> and <span class="italic">v</span> represent the elastic constant and the Poisson's ratio of the double-layer Na adsorption system, respectively.</span></span></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>
      
    
    
      
      <h2 id="sect960"><span class="a_heading">4. Conclusions</span></h2>
      <span>To better understand the mechanism of the MXene pillaring effect affecting the sodium storage performance, the adsorption, diffusion and mechanical properties of Na atoms in both Ti<small><sub>2</sub></small>CO<small><sub>2</sub></small> and Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> structures at a different spacing of MXene layers were investigated by enforcing the first-principles method. Overall, our results show that changes in the MXene layer spacing have different effects on the adsorption and diffusion of Na atoms, and suggest that the layer spacing should be in an appropriate range to make MXene play the best role in sodium storage. From our calculated outcomes, it can be concluded that for single Na-atomic layer adsorption, the optimum MXene layer spacing was 4  for both Ti<small><sub>2</sub></small>CO<small><sub>2</sub></small> and Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small>. In addition, as the MXene interlayer spacing was greater than 5 , the MXene interlayer can accommodate bilayers of Na adsorption, while the optimum MXene layer spacing was 7  and 6  for the Ti<small><sub>2</sub></small>CO<small><sub>2</sub></small> and Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> structures, respectively. Furthermore, it was found that not only the spacing between MXene layers, but also the stacking mode between MXene layers affected the adsorption and diffusion of Na, especially the diffusion of Na in the MXene interlayer. The calculated results show that, for both Ti<small><sub>2</sub></small>CO<small><sub>2</sub></small> and Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> configurations, when the stacking mode was CTi, the diffusion energy barrier of Na was greatly reduced. Our results also show that the adsorption and diffusion of Na and the mechanical properties of the system were not changed significantly when the MXene interlayer spacing was more than 8 . Finally, by considering various factors, the most suitable interlayer spacing of Ti<small><sub>2</sub></small>CO<small><sub>2</sub></small> and Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> for Na storage was 7  and 6 , respectively. Our study provides a useful theoretical basis for understanding the MXene pillar effect and contributes to the development of anode materials for SIBs.</span>

They are usually only set in response to actions made by you which amount to a request for services, such as setting your privacy preferences, logging in or filling in forms. You can set your browser to block or alert you about these cookies, but some parts of the site will not then work. These cookies do not store any personally identifiable information.</p></div></div><div class="ot-accordion-layout ot-cat-item ot-vs-config" data-optanongroupid="C0002"><button aria-expanded="false" ot-accordion="true" aria-controls="ot-desc-id-C0002" aria-labelledby="ot-header-id-C0002"></button><!-- Accordion header --><div class="ot-acc-hdr"><div class="ot-plus-minus"><span></span><span></span></div><h4 class="ot-cat-header" id="ot-header-id-C0002">Analytical cookies</h4><div class="ot-tgl"><input type="checkbox" name="ot-group-id-C0002" id="ot-group-id-C0002" role="switch" class="category-switch-handler" data-optanongroupid="C0002" aria-labelledby="ot-header-id-C0002"> <label class="ot-switch" for="ot-group-id-C0002"><span class="ot-switch-nob"></span> <span class="ot-label-txt">Analytical cookies</span></label> </div></div><!-- accordion detail --><div class="ot-acc-grpcntr ot-acc-txt"><p class="ot-acc-grpdesc ot-category-desc" id="ot-desc-id-C0002">These cookies allow us to count visits and traffic sources so we can measure and improve the performance of our site. They help us to know which pages are the most and least popular and see how visitors move around the site. All information these cookies collect is aggregated and therefore anonymous.
